href="/wiki/Serco_Marine_Services" title="Serco Marine Services">Marine Services</a></li></ul>\n</div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Royal_Navy" title="Template:Royal Navy"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Royal_Navy" title="Template talk:Royal Navy"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Royal Navy</b> (<b>RN</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">naval warfare force</a>. Although warships were used by the English kings from the early medieval period, the first major maritime engagements were fought in the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a>. The modern Royal Navy traces its origins to the early 16th century; the oldest of the UK\'s armed services, it is known as the <b>Senior Service</b>.\n</p><p>From the middle decades of the 17th century, and through the 18th century, the Royal Navy vied with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Navy">Dutch Navy</a> and later with the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> for maritime supremacy. From the mid 18th century, it was the world\'s most powerful navy until surpassed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The Royal Navy played a key part in establishing the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">unmatched world power</a> during the 19th and first part of the 20th centuries. Due to this historical prominence, it is common, even among non-Britons, to refer to it as "the Royal Navy" without qualification.\n</p><p>Following <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the Royal Navy was significantly reduced in size,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> although at the onset of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> it was still the world\'s largest. By the end of the war, however, the United States Navy had emerged as the world\'s largest. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the Royal Navy transformed into a primarily <a href="/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare" title="Anti-submarine warfare">anti-submarine force</a>, hunting for <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> submarines and mostly active in the <a href="/wiki/GIUK_gap" title="GIUK gap">GIUK gap</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">collapse of the Soviet Union</a>, its focus has returned to <a href="/wiki/Expeditionary_warfare" title="Expeditionary warfare">expeditionary</a> operations <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">around the world</a> and remains one of the world\'s foremost <a href="/wiki/Blue-water_navy" title="Blue-water navy">blue-water navies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> However, twenty-first century reductions in naval spending have led to a personnel shortage and a reduction in the number of warships.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Royal Navy maintains a fleet of technologically sophisticated ships and submarines<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> including an <a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)" title="HMS Queen Elizabeth (R08)">aircraft carrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albion-class_landing_platform_dock" title="Albion-class landing platform dock">two amphibious transport docks</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanguard-class">ballistic missile submarines</a> (which maintain the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear weapons and the United Kingdom">UK\'s nuclear deterrent</a>), six <a href="/wiki/Fleet_submarine" title="Fleet submarine">nuclear fleet submarines</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">guided missile destroyers</a>, 13 <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">frigates</a>, 13 <a href="/wiki/Mine-countermeasure_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mine-countermeasure vessel">mine-countermeasure vessels</a> and 22 <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol vessels</a>. As of April 2018, there are <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Royal_Navy_ships" title="List of active Royal Navy ships">74 commissioned ships</a> (including submarines) in the Royal Navy, plus 11 ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fleet_Auxiliary" title="Royal Fleet Auxiliary">Royal Fleet Auxiliary</a> (RFA); there are also five <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Navy_(United_Kingdom)" title="Merchant Navy (United Kingdom)">Merchant Navy ships</a> available to the RFA under a <a href="/wiki/Private_finance_initiative" title="Private finance initiative">private finance initiative</a>. The RFA replenishes Royal Navy warships at sea, and augments the Royal Navy\'s amphibious warfare capabilities through its three <a href="/wiki/Bay-class_landing_ship" title="Bay-class landing ship">Bay-class</a> landing ship vessels. It also works as a force multiplier for the Royal Navy, often doing patrols that frigates used to do. The total displacement of the Royal Navy is approximately 407,000 <a href="/wiki/Tonnes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> (705,004 tonnes including the Royal Fleet Auxiliary and Royal Marines).\n</p><p>The Royal Navy is part of <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Naval_Service" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Naval Service">Her Majesty\'s Naval Service</a>, which also includes the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a>. The professional head of the Naval Service is the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a> who is an <a href="/wiki/Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral (United Kingdom)">admiral</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Defence Council of the United Kingdom">Defence Council of the United Kingdom</a>. The Defence Council delegates management of the Naval Service to the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Board_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiralty Board (United Kingdom)">Admiralty Board</a>, chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Secretary of State for Defence</a>. The Royal Navy operates three bases in the United Kingdom where commissioned ships are based; <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">Clyde</a> and <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport</a>, the last being the largest operational naval base in Western Europe.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">Video clips</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role">Role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As the seaborne branch of <a href="/wiki/British_Armed_Forces" title="British Armed Forces">HM Armed Forces</a>, the RN has various roles. As it stands today, the RN has stated its 6 major roles as detailed below in umbrella terms.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Preventing Conflict \xe2\x80\x93 On a global and regional level</li>\n<li>Providing Security At Sea \xe2\x80\x93 To ensure the stability of international trade at sea</li>\n<li>International Partnerships \xe2\x80\x93 To help cement the relationship with the United Kingdom\'s allies (such as NATO)</li>\n<li>Maintaining a Readiness To Fight \xe2\x80\x93 To protect the United Kingdom\'s interests across the globe</li>\n<li>Protecting the Economy \xe2\x80\x93 To safe guard vital trade routes to guarantee the United Kingdom\'s and its allies\' economic prosperity at sea</li>\n<li>Providing Humanitarian Aid \xe2\x80\x93 To deliver a fast and effective response to global catastrophes</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="History of the Royal Navy">History of the Royal Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scots_Navy" title="Royal Scots Navy">Royal Scots Navy</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_navies_in_England_and_Scotland">Development of navies in England and Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development of navies in England and Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The strength of the fleet of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> was an important element in the kingdom\'s power in the 10th century.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> At one point <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelred_the_Unready" title="\xc3\x86thelred the Unready">Aethelred II</a> had an especially large fleet built by a national levy of one ship for every 310 <a href="/wiki/Hide_(unit)" title="Hide (unit)">hides</a> of land, but it is uncertain whether this was a standard or exceptional model for raising fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> During the period of Danish rule in the 11th century, the authorities maintained a standing fleet by taxation, and this continued for a time under the restored English regime of <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a> (reigned 1042\xe2\x80\x931066), who frequently commanded fleets in person.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleofSluys.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/220px-BattleofSluys.jpeg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/330px-BattleofSluys.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleofSluys.jpeg/440px-BattleofSluys.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1665" data-file-height="1560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleofSluys.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sluys" title="Battle of Sluys">Battle of Sluys</a> as depicted in <a href="/wiki/Froissart%27s_Chronicles" title="Froissart&#39;s Chronicles">Froissart\'s Chronicles</a>; late 14th century</div></div></div>\n<p>English naval power seemingly declined as a result of the Norman conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Medieval fleets, in England as elsewhere, were almost entirely composed of merchant ships enlisted into naval service in time of war. From time to time a few "king\'s ships" owned by the monarch were built for specifically warlike purposes; but, unlike some European states, England did not maintain a small permanent core of warships in peacetime. England\'s naval organisation was haphazard and the mobilisation of fleets when war broke out was slow.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the Viking era at an end, and conflict with France largely confined to the French lands of the English monarchy, England faced little threat from the sea during the 12th and 13th centuries, but in the 14th century the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a> dramatically increased the French menace. Early in the war French plans for an invasion of England failed when <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III of England</a> destroyed the French fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sluys" title="Battle of Sluys">Battle of Sluys</a> in 1340.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Major fighting was thereafter confined to French soil and England\'s naval capabilities sufficed to transport armies and supplies safely to their continental destinations. However, while subsequent French invasion schemes came to nothing, England\'s naval forces could not prevent frequent raids on the south-coast ports by the French and their <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian</a> allies. Such raids halted finally only with the occupation of northern France by <a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> deserves a large share of credit in fostering sea power. He embarked on a program of building merchant ships larger than heretofore. He also invested in dockyards, and commissioned the oldest surviving <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a> in 1495 at <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are mentions in medieval records of fleets commanded by Scottish kings including <a href="/wiki/William_the_Lion" title="William the Lion">William the Lion</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tytler1829pp309-10_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tytler1829pp309-10-24">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Scotland" title="Alexander II of Scotland">Alexander II</a>. The latter took personal command of a large naval force which sailed from the Firth of Clyde and anchored off the island of Kerrera in 1249, intended to transport his army in a campaign against the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Isles" title="Kingdom of the Isles">Kingdom of the Isles</a>, but he died before the campaign could begin.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macquarrie2004p147_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macquarrie2004p147-26">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> naval power was disrupted by conflicts between the Scandinavian kingdoms, but entered a period of resurgence in the 13th century when Norwegian kings began to build some of the largest ships seen in Northern European waters. These included king <a href="/wiki/Hakon_Hakonsson" class="mw-redirect" title="Hakon Hakonsson">Hakon Hakonsson</a>\'s <i>Krists\xc3\xba\xc3\xb0in</i>, built at Bergen from 1262\xe2\x80\x9363, which was 260 feet (79&#160;m) long, of 37 rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 1263 Hakon responded to <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Scotland" title="Alexander III of Scotland">Alexander III</a>\'s designs on the Hebrides by personally leading a major fleet of forty vessels, including the <i>Krists\xc3\xba\xc3\xb0in</i>, to the islands, where they were boosted by local allies to as many as 200 ships.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Records indicate that Alexander had several large oared ships built at <a href="/wiki/Ayr" title="Ayr">Ayr</a>, but he avoided a sea battle.<sup id="cite_ref-Tytler1829pp309-10_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tytler1829pp309-10-24">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Defeat on land at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Largs" title="Battle of Largs">Battle of Largs</a> and winter storms forced the Norwegian fleet to return home, leaving the Scottish crown as the major power in the region and leading to the ceding of the Western Isles to Alexander in 1266.<sup id="cite_ref-Macquarrie2004p153_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macquarrie2004p153-29">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>English naval power was vital to King <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I</a>\'s successful campaigns in Scotland from 1296, using largely merchant ships from England, Ireland and his allies in the Islands to transport and supply his armies.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger1997pp74-90_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger1997pp74-90-30">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Part of the reason for <a href="/wiki/Robert_I_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert I of Scotland">Robert I</a>\'s success was his ability to call on naval forces from the Islands. As a result of the expulsion of the Flemings from England in 1303, he gained the support of a major naval power in the North Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger1997pp74-90_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger1997pp74-90-30">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The development of naval power allowed Robert to successfully defeat English attempts to capture him in the Highlands and Islands and to blockade major English controlled fortresses at Perth and Stirling, the last forcing King <a href="/wiki/Edward_II_of_England" title="Edward II of England">Edward II</a> to attempt the relief that resulted at English defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bannockburn" title="Battle of Bannockburn">Bannockburn</a> in 1314.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger1997pp74-90_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger1997pp74-90-30">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Scottish naval forces allowed invasions of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> in 1313 and 1317 and Ireland in 1315. They were also crucial in the blockade of <a href="/wiki/Berwick-upon-Tweed" title="Berwick-upon-Tweed">Berwick</a>, which led to its fall in 1318.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger1997pp74-90_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger1997pp74-90-30">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the establishment of Scottish independence, King <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert I</a> turned his attention to building up a Scottish naval capacity. This was largely focused on the west coast, with the Exchequer Rolls of 1326 recording the feudal duties of his vassals in that region to aid him with their vessels and crews. Towards the end of his reign he supervised the building of at least one royal <a href="/wiki/Man-of-war" title="Man-of-war">man-of-war</a> near his palace at <a href="/wiki/Cardross,_Argyll_and_Bute" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardross, Argyll and Bute">Cardross</a> on the <a href="/wiki/River_Clyde" title="River Clyde">River Clyde</a>. In the late 14th century naval warfare with England was conducted largely by hired Scots, Flemish and French merchantmen and privateers.<sup id="cite_ref-Grant_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grant-31">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Scotland" title="James I of Scotland">James I of Scotland</a> (1394\xe2\x80\x931437, reigned 1406\xe2\x80\x931437), took a greater interest in naval power. After his return to Scotland in 1424, he established a shipbuilding yard at <a href="/wiki/Leith" title="Leith">Leith</a>, a house for marine stores, and a workshop. King\'s ships were built and equipped there to be used for trade as well as war, one of which accompanied him on his expedition to the Islands in 1429. The office of <a href="/wiki/Lord_High_Admiral_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord High Admiral of Scotland">Lord High Admiral</a> was probably founded in this period.<sup id="cite_ref-Grant_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grant-31">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> It would soon become a hereditary office, in the control of the <a href="/wiki/Earls_of_Bothwell" class="mw-redirect" title="Earls of Bothwell">Earls of Bothwell</a> in the 15th and 16th centuries and the <a href="/wiki/Earls_of_Lennox" class="mw-redirect" title="Earls of Lennox">Earls of Lennox</a> in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Murdoch2010p10_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murdoch2010p10-32">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>King <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_Scotland" title="James II of Scotland">James II</a> (1430\xe2\x80\x931460, reigned 1437\xe2\x80\x931460) is known to have purchased a <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravel</a> by 1449.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger2004pp166-7_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger2004pp166-7-33">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Around 1476 the Scottish merchant John Barton received <a href="/wiki/Letters_of_marque" class="mw-redirect" title="Letters of marque">letters of marque</a> that allowed him to gain compensation for the capture of his vessels by the Portuguese by capturing ships under their colours. These letters would be repeated to his three sons John, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Barton_(privateer)" title="Andrew Barton (privateer)">Andrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Barton_of_Over_Barnton" title="Robert Barton of Over Barnton">Robert</a>, who would play a major part in the Scottish naval effort into the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In his struggles with his nobles in 1488 <a href="/wiki/James_III_of_Scotland" title="James III of Scotland">James III</a> (r. 1451\xe2\x80\x9388) received assistance from his two warships the <i>Flower</i> and the <i>King\'s Carvel</i> also known as the <i>Yellow Carvel</i>, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Wood_of_Largo" title="Andrew Wood of Largo">Andrew Wood of Largo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grant_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grant-31">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> After the king\'s death Wood served his son <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV</a> (r. 1488\xe2\x80\x931513), defeating an English incursion into the <a href="/wiki/River_Forth" title="River Forth">Forth</a> by five English ships in 1489 and three more heavily armed English ships off the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tay" title="River Tay">River Tay</a> the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1500.E2.80.931707"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1500\xe2\x80\x931707">1500\xe2\x80\x931707</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1500\xe2\x80\x931707">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Invincible_Armada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/220px-Invincible_Armada.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/330px-Invincible_Armada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Invincible_Armada.jpg/440px-Invincible_Armada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1956" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Invincible_Armada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A late <a href="/wiki/16th_century" title="16th century">16th-century</a> painting of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> in battle with English warships</div></div></div><p>A standing "Navy Royal",<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> with its own secretariat, dockyards and a permanent core of purpose-built warships, emerged during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I</a> England became involved in a war with Spain, which saw privately owned vessels combining with the Queen\'s ships in highly profitable raids against Spanish commerce and colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1588, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> sent the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> against England to end English support for Dutch rebels, to stop English <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">corsair</a> activity and to depose the Protestant Elizabeth I and restore Catholicism to England. The Spaniards sailed from <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, planning to escort an invasion force from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a> but the scheme failed due to poor planning, English harrying, blocking action by the Dutch, and severe storms.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> A major English expedition the following year was intended by Elizabeth to destroy the survivors of the Spanish fleet, but instead dissipated its efforts in unsuccessful schemes to intercept a Spanish treasure convoy or foment revolt against Spanish rule in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the early 17th century, England\'s relative naval power deteriorated, and there were increasing raids by <a href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary corsairs">Barbary corsairs</a> on ships and English coastal communities to capture people as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, which the Navy had little success in countering.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> undertook a major programme of warship building, creating a small force of powerful ships, but his methods of fundraising to finance the fleet contributed to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In the wake of this conflict and the abolition of the monarchy, the new <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a>, isolated and threatened from all sides, dramatically expanded the Navy, which became the most powerful in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Scheveningen_(Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde)(Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Scheveningen_%28Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde%29%28Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5950" data-file-height="3680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Scheveningen_(Slag_bij_Ter_Heijde)(Jan_Abrahamsz._Beerstraten).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Scheveningen" title="Battle of Scheveningen">Battle of Scheveningen</a> in 1653</div></div></div>\n<p>The new regime\'s introduction of <a href="/wiki/Navigation_Acts" title="Navigation Acts">Navigation Acts</a>, providing that all merchant shipping to and from England or her colonies should be carried out by English ships, led to war with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In the early stages of this <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="First Anglo-Dutch War">First Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1652\xe2\x80\x931654), the superiority of the large, heavily armed English ships was offset by superior Dutch tactical organisation and the fighting was inconclusive.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> English tactical improvements resulted in a series of crushing victories in 1653 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Portland" title="Battle of Portland">Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Gabbard" title="Battle of the Gabbard">the Gabbard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Scheveningen" title="Battle of Scheveningen">Scheveningen</a>, bringing peace on favourable terms.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This was the first war fought largely, on the English side, by purpose-built, state-owned warships. It was followed by a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1654-1660)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1654-1660)">war with Spain</a>, which saw the English conquest of <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> in 1655 and successful attacks on Spanish treasure fleets in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cadiz_(1656)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Cadiz (1656)">1656</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(1657)" title="Battle of Santa Cruz de Tenerife (1657)">1657</a>, but also the devastation of English merchant shipping by the <a href="/wiki/Dunkirkers" title="Dunkirkers">privateers of Dunkirk</a>, until their home port was captured by Anglo-French forces in 1658.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">English monarchy</a> was restored in May 1660, and <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> assumed the throne. One of his first acts was to re-establish the <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">Navy</a>, but from this point on, it ceased to be the personal possession of the reigning monarch, and instead became a national institution\xe2\x80\x94with the title of "The Royal Navy".<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of their defeat in the First Anglo-Dutch War, the Dutch transformed their navy, largely abandoning the use of militarised merchantmen and establishing a fleet composed mainly of heavily armed, purpose-built warships, as the English had done previously. Consequently, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1665\xe2\x80\x931667) was a closely fought struggle between evenly matched opponents, with English victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lowestoft" title="Battle of Lowestoft">Lowestoft</a> (1665) countered by Dutch triumph in the epic <a href="/wiki/Four_Days_Battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Four Days Battle">Four Days Battle</a> (1666).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The deadlock was broken not by combat but by the superiority of Dutch public finance, as in 1667 Charles II was forced to lay up the fleet in port for lack of money to keep it at sea, while negotiating for peace. Disaster followed, as the Dutch fleet mounted the <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_the_Medway" title="Raid on the Medway">Raid on the Medway</a>, breaking into <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Dockyard" title="Chatham Dockyard">Chatham Dockyard</a> and capturing or burning many of the Navy\'s largest ships at their moorings.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1672\xe2\x80\x931674), Charles II allied with <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a> against the Dutch, but the combined Anglo-French fleet was fought to a standstill in a series of inconclusive battles, while the French invasion by land was warded off.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_(Peter_van_de_Velde).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/220px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/330px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg/440px-Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_%28Peter_van_de_Velde%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1974" data-file-height="1294" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Het_verbranden_van_de_Engelse_vloot_voor_Chatham_-_The_Dutch_burn_down_the_English_fleet_before_Chatham_-_June_20_1667_(Peter_van_de_Velde).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dutch <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_the_Medway" title="Raid on the Medway">Raid on the Medway</a> in 1667 during the Second Anglo\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War</div></div></div>\n<p>During the 1670s and 1680s, the English Royal Navy succeeded in permanently ending the threat to English shipping from the Barbary corsairs, inflicting defeats which induced the Barbary states to conclude long-lasting peace treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1688, England joined the European coalition against Louis XIV in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Grand_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Grand Alliance">War of the Grand Alliance</a> (1688\xe2\x80\x931697). Louis\' recent shipbuilding programme had given France the largest navy in Europe. A combined Anglo-Dutch fleet was defeated at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Beachy_Head_(1690)" title="Battle of Beachy Head (1690)">Beachy Head</a> (1690), but victory at <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Barfleur_and_La_Hogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Battles of Barfleur and La Hogue">Barfleur-La Hogue</a> (1692) was a turning-point, marking the end of France\'s brief pre-eminence at sea and the beginning of an enduring English, later British, supremacy.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the course of the 17th century, the English Royal Navy completed the transition from a semi-amateur Navy Royal fighting in conjunction with private vessels into a fully professional institution. Its financial provisions were gradually regularised, it came to rely on dedicated warships only, and it developed a professional officer corps with a defined career structure, superseding an earlier mix of "gentlemen" (upper-class soldiers) and "tarpaulins" (professional seamen, who generally served on merchant or fishing vessels in peacetime).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>James IV put the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Scots_Navy" title="Royal Scots Navy">Royal Scots Navy</a> on a new footing, founding a harbour at <a href="/wiki/Newhaven,_Edinburgh" title="Newhaven, Edinburgh">Newhaven</a> in May 1504, and two years later ordering the construction of a dockyard at the Pools of <a href="/wiki/Airth" title="Airth">Airth</a>. The upper reaches of the Forth were protected by new fortifications on <a href="/wiki/Inchgarvie" title="Inchgarvie">Inchgarvie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Scottish ships had some success against privateers, accompanied the king in his expeditions in the islands and intervened in conflicts in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grantppi-xii_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantppi-xii-56">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Expeditions to the Highlands to Islands to curb the power of the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Donald" title="Clan Donald">MacDonald</a> <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Isles" title="Lord of the Isles">Lord of the Isles</a> were largely ineffective until in 1504 the king accompanied a squadron under Wood heavily armed with artillery, which battered the MacDonald strongholds into submission. Since some of these island fortresses could only be attacked from seaward, naval historian N. A. M. Rodger has suggested this may have marked the end of medieval naval warfare in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>, ushering in a new tradition of <a href="/wiki/Naval_artillery_in_the_Age_of_Sail" title="Naval artillery in the Age of Sail">artillery warfare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger2004pp166-7_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger2004pp166-7-33">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The king acquired a total of 38 ships for the Royal Scottish Navy, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Scottish_warship_Margaret" title="Scottish warship Margaret">Margaret</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Michael_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael (ship)">Michael</a></i> or <i>Great Michael</i>, the largest warship of its time (1511).<sup id="cite_ref-Smout1992p45_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smout1992p45-57">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The latter, built at great expense at Newhaven and launched in 1511, was 240 feet (73&#160;m) in length, weighed 1,000&#160;tons, had 24 cannon, and was, at that time, the largest ship in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smout1992p45_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smout1992p45-57">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-S._Murdoch,_2010_pp._33-4_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S._Murdoch,_2010_pp._33-4-58">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> It marked a shift in designed as it was designed specifically to carry a main armament of heavy artillery.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger2004pp166-7_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger2004pp166-7-33">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="3998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:An_English_Ship_in_Action_with_Barbary_Vessels_RMG_BHC0893.tiff" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An English ship battles with a <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary ship</a> and two galleys in <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> in 1676</div></div></div>\n<p>During the Rough Wooing, the attempt to force a marriage between James V\'s heir <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a>\'s son, the future <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward VI">Edward VI</a>, in 1542, the <i>Mary Willoughby</i>, the <i>Lion</i>, and the <i>Salamander</i> under the command of John Barton, son of Robert Barton, attacked merchants and fishermen off <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a>. They later blockaded a London merchant ship called the <i>Antony of Bruges</i> in a creek on the coast of Brittany.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 1544, Edinburgh was attacked by an <a href="/wiki/Burning_of_Edinburgh_(1544)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burning of Edinburgh (1544)">English marine force and burnt</a>. The <i>Salamander</i> and the Scottish-built <i>Unicorn</i> were captured at Leith. The Scots still had two royal naval vessels and numerous smaller private vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When, as a result of the series of international treaties, Charles V declared war upon Scotland in 1544, the Scots were able to engage in a highly profitable campaign of privateering that lasted six years and the gains of which probably outweighed the losses in trade with the Low Countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson2007pp181-2_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson2007pp181-2-61">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Scots operated in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> from the 1540s, joining the French in the capture of <a href="/wiki/Borburata" title="Borburata">Burburuta</a> in 1567.<sup id="cite_ref-Murdoch2010p172_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murdoch2010p172-62">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> English and Scottish naval warfare and privateering broke out sporadically in the 1550s.<sup id="cite_ref-Rodger2004p197_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rodger2004p197-63">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> When Anglo-Scottish relations deteriorated again in 1557 as part of a wider <a href="/wiki/Italian_War_of_1551%E2%80%9359" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian War of 1551\xe2\x80\x9359">war between Spain and France</a>, small ships called \'shallops\' were noted between Leith and France, passing as fishermen, but bringing munitions and money. Private merchant ships were rigged at Leith, Aberdeen and <a href="/wiki/Dundee" title="Dundee">Dundee</a> as men-of-war, and the regent Mary of Guise claimed English prizes, one over 200 tons, for her fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The re-fitted <i>Mary Willoughby</i> sailed with 11 other ships against Scotland in August 1557, landing troops and six field guns on <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> to attack the <a href="/wiki/Kirkwall_Castle" title="Kirkwall Castle">Kirkwall Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Magnus_Cathedral" title="St Magnus Cathedral">St Magnus Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_Palace,_Kirkwall" title="Bishop&#39;s Palace, Kirkwall">Bishop\'s Palace</a>. The English were repulsed by a Scottish force numbering 3000, and the English vice-admiral <a href="/wiki/John_Clere_(c._1511%E2%80%9357)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Clere (c. 1511\xe2\x80\x9357)">Sir John Clere</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ormesby_St_Margaret_with_Scratby" title="Ormesby St Margaret with Scratby">Ormesby</a> was killed, but none of the English ships were lost.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paton,_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg/220px-Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg/330px-Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg/440px-Paton%2C_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paton,_Battle_of_Barfleur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Barfleur" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Barfleur">Battle of Barfleur</a> in 1692</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Crowns" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Crowns">Union of Crowns</a> in 1603 conflict between Scotland and England ended, but Scotland found itself involved in England\'s foreign policy, opening up Scottish shipping to attack. In the 1620s, Scotland found herself fighting a naval war as England\'s ally, first <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1625)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1625)">against Spain</a> and then also <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_War_(1627%E2%80%931629)" title="Anglo-French War (1627\xe2\x80\x931629)">against France</a>, while simultaneously embroiled in undeclared North Sea commitments in the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War#Danish_intervention_(1625\xe2\x80\x931629)" title="Thirty Years&#39; War">Danish intervention in the Thirty Years\' War</a>. In 1626 a squadron of three ships was bought and equipped, at a cost of least \xc2\xa35,200 sterling, to guard against privateers operating out of Spanish-controlled <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a> and other ships were armed in preparation for potential action.<sup id="cite_ref-S._Murdoch,_2010_pp._33-4_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S._Murdoch,_2010_pp._33-4-58">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The acting High Admiral <a href="/wiki/John_Gordon,_1st_Viscount_of_Kenmure" title="John Gordon, 1st Viscount of Kenmure">John Gordon of Lochinvar</a> organised as many as three <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">marque fleets</a> of privateers.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It was probably one of Lochinvar\'s marque fleets that was sent to support the English Royal Navy in defending Irish waters in 1626.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 1627, the Royal Scots Navy and accompanying contingents of burgh privateers participated in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saint-Martin-de-R%C3%A9_(1627)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Saint-Martin-de-R\xc3\xa9 (1627)">major expedition to Biscay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The Scots also returned to the West Indies, with Lochinvar taking French prizes and founding the colony of <a href="/wiki/Floreana_Island" title="Floreana Island">Charles Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Murdoch2010p172_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murdoch2010p172-62">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In 1629, two squadrons of privateers led by Lochinvar and William Lord Alexander, sailed for Canada, taking part in the campaign that resulted in the capture of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> from the French, which was handed back after the subsequent peace.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1697 the English Royal Navy had 323 warships, while Scotland was still dependent on merchantman and privateers. In the 1690s, two separate schemes for larger naval forces were put in motion. As usual, the larger part was played by the merchant community rather than the government. The first was the <a href="/wiki/Darien_Scheme" class="mw-redirect" title="Darien Scheme">Darien Scheme</a> to found a Scottish colony in Spanish controlled America. It was undertaken by the <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Scotland" title="Company of Scotland">Company of Scotland</a>, who created a fleet of five ships, including the <i>Caledonia</i> and the <i>St. Andrew</i>, all built or chartered in Holland and Hamburg. It sailed to the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Darien" class="mw-redirect" title="Isthmus of Darien">Isthmus of Darien</a> in 1698, but the venture failed and only one ship returned to Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In the same period it was decided to establish a professional navy for the protection of commerce in home waters during the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Years%27_War" title="Nine Years&#39; War">Nine Years\' War</a> (1688\xe2\x80\x9397) with France, with three purpose-built warships bought from English shipbuilders in 1696. These were the <i>Royal William</i>, a 32-gun <a href="/wiki/Fifth_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fifth rate">fifth rate</a> and two smaller ships, the <i>Royal Mary</i> and the <i>Dumbarton Castle</i>, each of 24 guns, generally described as frigates.<sup id="cite_ref-Grantp48_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantp48-71">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Development_of_Britain.27s_navy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_Britain\'s_navy">Development of Britain\'s navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development of Britain&#039;s navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="1707.E2.80.931815"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1707\xe2\x80\x931815">1707\xe2\x80\x931815</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1707\xe2\x80\x931815">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/170px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/255px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg/340px-HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2250" data-file-height="2952" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory_-_bow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS&#160;<i>Victory</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio Nelson">Nelson</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a>, is still a <a href="/wiki/Ship_commissioning" title="Ship commissioning">commissioned</a> Royal Navy ship, although she is now permanently kept in <a href="/wiki/Dry-dock" class="mw-redirect" title="Dry-dock">dry-dock</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a>, which created the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> in 1707, established the Royal Navy of the newly united kingdom. The Scots office of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lord_High_Admirals_of_Scotland" title="List of Lord High Admirals of Scotland">Lord High Admiral</a> was subsumed within the office of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lords_High_Admiral" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Lords High Admiral">Admiral of Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Murdoch2010p10_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murdoch2010p10-32">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The three vessels of the small Royal Scottish Navy were transferred to the Royal Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-Grantp48_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grantp48-71">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout the 18th and 19th centuries, the Royal Navy was the largest maritime force in the world, but until 1805 combinations of enemies repeatedly matched or exceeded its forces in numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, it was able to maintain an almost uninterrupted ascendancy over its rivals through superiority in financing, tactics, training, organisation, social cohesion, hygiene, dockyard facilities, logistical support and (from the middle of the 18th century) warship design and construction.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> (1702\xe2\x80\x931714), the Navy operated in conjunction with the Dutch against the navies of France and Spain, in support of the efforts of Britain\'s Austrian <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> allies to seize control of Spain and its Mediterranean dependencies from the <a href="/wiki/Bourbons" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbons">Bourbons</a>. Amphibious operations by the Anglo-Dutch fleet brought about the capture of <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> and a number of Spanish mainland ports, most importantly <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. While most of these gains were turned over to the Habsburgs, Britain held on to <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>, which were retained in the peace settlement, providing the Navy with Mediterranean bases. Early in the war French naval squadrons had done considerable damage to English and Dutch commercial convoys. However, a major victory over France and Spain at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vigo_Bay" title="Battle of Vigo Bay">Vigo Bay</a> (1702), further successes in battle, and the scuttling of the entire French Mediterranean fleet at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a> in 1707 virtually cleared the Navy\'s opponents from the seas for the latter part of the war. Naval operations also enabled the conquest of the French colonies in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Further conflict with Spain followed in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Quadruple_Alliance" title="War of the Quadruple Alliance">War of the Quadruple Alliance</a> (1718\xe2\x80\x931720), in which the Navy helped thwart a Spanish attempt to regain <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> from Austria and <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a>, defeating a Spanish fleet at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Passaro" title="Battle of Cape Passaro">Cape Passaro</a> (1718), and in an undeclared war in the 1720s, in which Spain tried to retake <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/220px-LindsayCambridge.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/330px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/440px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="952" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Cuba">British expedition against Cuba</a> in 1762</div></div></div>\n<p>After a period of relative peace, the Navy became engaged in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins&#39; Ear">War of Jenkins\' Ear</a> (1739\xe2\x80\x931748) against Spain, which was dominated by a series of costly and mostly unsuccessful attacks on Spanish ports in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, primarily a huge expedition against <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_de_Indias" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena de Indias</a> in 1741. These led to heavy loss of life from tropical diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 1742 the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">Kingdom of the Two Sicilies</a> was driven to withdraw from the war in the space of half an hour by the threat of a bombardment of its capital <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> by a small British squadron. The war became subsumed in the wider <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> (1744\xe2\x80\x931748), once again pitting Britain against France. Naval fighting in this war, which for the first time included major operations in the Indian Ocean, was largely inconclusive, the most significant event being the failure of <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_invasion_of_Britain_(1744)" title="Planned French invasion of Britain (1744)">an attempted French invasion of England</a> in 1744.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a> (1756\xe2\x80\x931763) saw the Navy conduct amphibious campaigns leading to the conquest of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>, of <a href="/wiki/List_of_French_possessions_and_colonies" title="List of French possessions and colonies">French colonies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, and of small islands off the French coast, while operations in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> contributed to the destruction of French power in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> A new French <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_invasion_of_Britain_(1759)" title="Planned French invasion of Britain (1759)">attempt to invade Britain</a> was thwarted by the defeat of their escort fleet in the extraordinary <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quiberon_Bay" title="Battle of Quiberon Bay">Battle of Quiberon Bay</a> in 1759, fought in a gale on a dangerous <a href="/wiki/Lee_shore" title="Lee shore">lee shore</a>. Once again the British fleet effectively eliminated the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> from the war, leading France to abandon major operations.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 1762 the resumption of hostilities with Spain led to the British capture of <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, along with a Spanish fleet sheltering there.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/250px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg" width="250" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/375px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg/500px-The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="589" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_battle_of_the_Saints_12_avril_1782.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Saintes" title="Battle of the Saintes">Battle of the Saintes</a> (1782). On the right, the French flagship, <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Ville_de_Paris_(1764)" title="French ship Ville de Paris (1764)">Ville de Paris</a></i>, in action against <a href="/wiki/HMS_Barfleur_(1768)" title="HMS Barfleur (1768)">HMS&#160;<i>Barfleur</i></a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a> (1775\xe2\x80\x931783) the Royal Navy readily obliterated the small <a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> fielded by the rebel colonists, but the entry of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, Spain and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> into the war against Britain produced a combination of opposing forces which deprived the Navy of its position of superiority for the first time since the 1690s, briefly but decisively. The war saw a series of inconclusive battles in the Atlantic and Caribbean, in which the Navy failed to achieve the decisive victories needed to secure the supply lines of British forces in North America and to cut off the colonial rebels from outside support.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The most important operation of the war came in 1781 when, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Chesapeake" title="Battle of the Chesapeake">Battle of the Chesapeake</a>, the British fleet failed to lift the French blockade of Lord Cornwallis\'s army, resulting in Cornwallis\'s surrender at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yorktown_(1781)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Yorktown (1781)">Yorktown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Although this disaster effectively concluded the fighting in North America, hostilities continued in the Indian Ocean, where the French were prevented from re-establishing a meaningful foothold in India, and in the Caribbean. British victory in the Caribbean in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Saintes" title="Battle of the Saintes">Battle of the Saintes</a> in 1782 and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cape_Spartel" title="Battle of Cape Spartel">relief of Gibraltar</a> later the same year symbolised the restoration of British naval ascendancy, but this came too late to prevent the independence of the rebellious <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/220px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/330px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg/440px-Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2102" data-file-height="1502" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombardement_of_Algiers_1816.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> in 1816 to support the ultimatum to release European slaves</div></div></div>\n<p>The eradication of scurvy from the Royal Navy in the 1790s came about due to the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Blane" title="Gilbert Blane">Gilbert Blane</a>, chairman of the Navy\'s <a href="/wiki/Sick_and_Hurt_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Sick and Hurt Board">Sick and Hurt Board</a>, which ordered fresh lemon juice to be given to sailors on ships. Other navies soon adopted this successful solution.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> (1793\xe2\x80\x931801) and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1803\xe2\x80\x931814 and 1815) saw the Royal Navy reach a peak of efficiency, dominating the navies of all Britain\'s adversaries, which spent most of the war blockaded in port. The Navy achieved an emphatic early victory at the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_First_of_June" title="Glorious First of June">Glorious First of June</a> (1794), and gained a number of smaller victories while supporting abortive French <a href="/wiki/Royalist" title="Royalist">Royalist</a> efforts to regain control of France. In the course of one such operation, the majority of the French Mediterranean fleet was captured or destroyed during a short-lived occupation of Toulon in 1793.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The military successes of the French Revolutionary r\xc3\xa9gime brought the Spanish and Dutch navies into the war on the French side, but the losses inflicted on the Dutch at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Camperdown" title="Battle of Camperdown">Battle of Camperdown</a> in 1797 and the surrender of their surviving fleet to a landing force at Den Helder in 1799 effectively eliminated the Dutch navy from the war.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spithead_and_Nore_mutinies" title="Spithead and Nore mutinies">Spithead and Nore mutinies</a> in 1797 incapacitated the Channel and North Sea fleets, leaving Britain potentially exposed to invasion, but were rapidly resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The British Mediterranean fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a> failed to intercept <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>\'s 1798 expedition to invade Egypt, but annihilated the French fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Nile" title="Battle of the Nile">Battle of the Nile</a>, leaving Bonaparte\'s army isolated.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The emergence of a Baltic coalition opposed to Britain led to an attack on Denmark, which lost much of its fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1801)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1801)">Battle of Copenhagen</a> (1801) and came to terms with Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trafalgar1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/280px-Trafalgar1.jpg" width="280" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/420px-Trafalgar1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Trafalgar1.jpg/560px-Trafalgar1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="645" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trafalgar1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a>, depicted here in its opening phase</div></div></div>\n<p>During these years, the Navy also conducted amphibious operations that captured most of the <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French Caribbean islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonies</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a>. Though successful in their outcome, the expeditions to the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, conducted on a grand scale, led to devastating losses from disease. Except for Ceylon and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, these gains were returned following the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amiens" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace of Amiens">Peace of Amiens</a> in 1802, which briefly halted the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Menorca, which had been repeatedly lost and regained during the 18th century, was restored to Spain, its place as the Navy\'s main base in the Mediterranean being taken by the new acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>. War resumed in 1803 and Napoleon attempted to assemble a large enough fleet from the French and Spanish squadrons blockaded in various ports to cover an invasion of England. The Navy frustrated these efforts, and following the abandonment of the invasion plan, Nelson defeated the combined Franco-Spanish fleet at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a> (1805).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Trafalgar, large-scale fighting at sea remained limited to the destruction of small, fugitive French squadrons, and amphibious operations which again captured the colonies which had been restored at Amiens, along with France\'s Indian Ocean base at <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Moluccas" class="mw-redirect" title="Moluccas">Moluccas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In 1807, French plans to seize the Danish fleet led to a pre-emptive British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1807)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1807)">attack on Copenhagen</a>, resulting in the surrender of the entire Danish navy.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impressment</a> of British and American sailors from American ships contributed to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> (1812\xe2\x80\x931814) against the United States, in which the naval fighting was largely confined to commerce raiding and single-ship actions.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The brief renewal of war after <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>\'s return to power in 1815 did not bring a resumption of naval combat.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1815.E2.80.931914"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1815\xe2\x80\x931914">1815\xe2\x80\x931914</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1815\xe2\x80\x931914">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Between 1815 and 1914, the Navy saw little serious action, owing to the absence of any opponent strong enough to challenge its dominance. During this period, naval warfare underwent a comprehensive transformation, brought about by steam propulsion, metal ship construction, and explosive munitions. Despite having to completely replace its war fleet, the Navy managed to maintain its overwhelming advantage over all potential rivals. Due to British leadership in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, the country enjoyed unparalleled shipbuilding capacity and financial resources, which ensured that no rival could take advantage of these revolutionary changes to negate the British advantage in ship numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9,137_tons,_Royal_Navy_(first_armour-plated,_iron-hulled_warship.)_(11632529933).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/220px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/330px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg/440px-HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9%2C137_tons%2C_Royal_Navy_%28first_armour-plated%2C_iron-hulled_warship.%29_%2811632529933%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1619" data-file-height="1084" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_armoured_frigate_9,137_tons,_Royal_Navy_(first_armour-plated,_iron-hulled_warship.)_(11632529933).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS&#160;<i>Warrior</i></a>, the first iron-hulled, armour-plated warship</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1859, the fleet was estimated to number about 1000 in all, including both combat and non-combat vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 1889, Parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Naval_Defence_Act_1889" title="Naval Defence Act 1889">Naval Defence Act</a>, which formally adopted the \'two-power standard\', which stipulated that the Royal Navy should maintain a number of battleships at least equal to the combined strength of the next two largest navies.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_ships_in_Canton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/220px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/330px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/British_ships_in_Canton.jpg/440px-British_ships_in_Canton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_ships_in_Canton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The British assault on <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a> during the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a> in 1841</div></div></div>\n<p>The first major action that the Royal Navy saw during this period was the <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> in 1816 by a joint Anglo-Dutch fleet under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Pellew,_1st_Viscount_Exmouth" title="Edward Pellew, 1st Viscount Exmouth">Lord Exmouth</a>, to force the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary states">Barbary state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Regency_of_Algiers" class="mw-redirect" title="Regency of Algiers">Algiers</a> to free <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> slaves and to halt the practice of enslaving <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a>.
