class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg/330px-Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg/440px-Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2570" data-file-height="1685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uknavy_agustawestland_eh-101_merlin_hm1_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Navy <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101" title="AgustaWestland AW101">EH-101 Merlin</a> at <a href="/wiki/RIAT" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAT">RIAT</a> 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>The current role of the Royal Navy is to protect British interests at home and abroad, executing the foreign and defence policies of Her Majesty\'s Government through the exercise of military effect, diplomatic activities and other activities in support of these objectives. The Royal Navy is also a key element of the British contribution to NATO, with a number of assets allocated to NATO tasks at any time.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> These objectives are delivered via a number of core capabilities:<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Maintenance of the UK Nuclear Deterrent through a policy of <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_class_submarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanguard class submarine"><i>Continuous at Sea Deterrence</i></a>.</li>\n<li>Provision of two medium scale <a href="/wiki/Carrier_battle_group" title="Carrier battle group">maritime task groups</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a>.</li>\n<li>Delivery of the UK <a href="/wiki/British_Commandos" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commandos">Commando</a> force.</li>\n<li>Contribution of assets to the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Helicopter_Command" title="Joint Helicopter Command">Joint Helicopter Command</a>.</li>\n<li>Maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">standing patrol commitments</a>.</li>\n<li>Provision of <a href="/wiki/Minehunter" title="Minehunter">mine counter measures</a> capability to United Kingdom and allied commitments.</li>\n<li>Provision of <a href="/wiki/Hydrography" title="Hydrography">hydrographic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meteorological" class="mw-redirect" title="Meteorological">meteorological</a> services deployable worldwide.</li>\n<li>Protection of Britain and EU\'s <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_deployments">Current deployments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Current deployments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">Standing Royal Navy deployments</a></div>\n<p>The Royal Navy is currently deployed in different areas of the world, including some <a href="/wiki/Standing_Royal_Navy_deployments" title="Standing Royal Navy deployments">standing Royal Navy deployments</a>. These include several home tasks as well as overseas deployments. The Navy is deployed in the Mediterranean as part of standing NATO deployments including mine countermeasures and NATO Maritime Group 2. In both the North and South Atlantic RN vessels are patrolling. There is always a Falkland Islands patrol vessel on deployment, currently <a href="/wiki/HMS_Clyde_(P257)" title="HMS Clyde (P257)">HMS&#160;<i>Clyde</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Royal Navy operates a <a href="/wiki/Response_Force_Task_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Response Force Task Group">Response Force Task Group</a> (a product of the 2010 Strategic Defence and Security Review), which is poised to respond globally to short-notice tasking across a range of defence activities, such as non-combatant evacuation operations, disaster relief, humanitarian aid or amphibious operations. In 2011, the first deployment of the task group occurred under the name \'COUGAR 11\' which saw them transit through the Mediterranean where they took part in multinational amphibious exercises before moving further east through the Suez Canal for further exercises in the Indian Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/220px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/330px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg/440px-RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RN_Flotilla_45154692.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The RN presence in the Persian Gulf typically consists of a Type 45 destroyer and a squadron of minehunters supported by an RFA <a href="/wiki/Bay-class_landing_ship" title="Bay-class landing ship">Bay-class</a> "mothership"</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, the RN sustains commitments in support of both national and coalition efforts to stabilise the region. The <a href="/wiki/Armilla_Patrol" class="mw-redirect" title="Armilla Patrol">Armilla Patrol</a>, which started in 1980, is the navy\'s primary commitment the Gulf region. The Royal Navy also contributes to the combined maritime forces in the Gulf in support of coalition operations.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The UK Maritime Component Commander, overseer of all of Her Majesty\'s warships in the Persian Gulf and surrounding waters, is also deputy commander of the Combined Maritime Forces.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Navy has been responsible for training the fledgling <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Navy" title="Iraqi Navy">Iraqi Navy</a> and securing Iraq\'s oil terminals following the cessation of hostilities in the country. The Iraqi Training and Advisory Mission (Navy) (Umm Qasr), headed by a Royal Navy captain, has been responsible for the former duty whilst Commander Task Force Iraqi Maritime, a Royal Navy commodore, has been responsible for the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Royal Navy contributes to standing NATO formations and maintains forces as part of the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Response_Force" title="NATO Response Force">NATO Response Force</a>. The RN also has a long-standing commitment to supporting the <a href="/wiki/Five_Powers_Defence_Arrangements" class="mw-redirect" title="Five Powers Defence Arrangements">Five Powers Defence Arrangements</a> countries and occasionally deploys to the Far East as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> This deployment typically consists of a <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">frigate</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Echo-class_survey_ship_(2002)" title="Echo-class survey ship (2002)">survey vessel</a>, operating separately. <a href="/wiki/Operation_Atalanta" title="Operation Atalanta">Operation Atalanta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>\'s anti-<a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> operation in the Indian Ocean, is permanently commanded by a senior Royal Navy or Royal Marines officer at <a href="/wiki/Northwood_Headquarters" title="Northwood Headquarters">Northwood Headquarters</a> and the navy contributes ships to the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Command.2C_control_and_organisation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Command,_control_and_organisation">Command, control and organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Command, control and organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The titular head of the Royal Navy is the <a href="/wiki/Lord_High_Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord High Admiral (United Kingdom)">Lord High Admiral</a>, a position which has been held by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">the Duke of Edinburgh</a> since 2011. The position had been held by Queen Elizabeth II from 1964 to 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">Sovereign</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief_of_the_British_Armed_Forces" title="Commander-in-chief of the British Armed Forces">Commander-in-chief of the British Armed Forces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The professional head of the Naval Service is the <a href="/wiki/First_Sea_Lord" title="First Sea Lord">First Sea Lord</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Admiral_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral (United Kingdom)">admiral</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Defence Council of the United Kingdom">Defence Council of the United Kingdom</a>. The Defence Council delegates management of the Naval Service to the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Board_(United_Kingdom)" title="Admiralty Board (United Kingdom)">Admiralty Board</a>, chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Secretary of State for Defence</a>, which directs the <a href="/wiki/Navy_Board" title="Navy Board">Navy Board</a>, a sub-committee of the Admiralty Board comprising only naval officers and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MOD) civil servants. These are all based in <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)#Property_portfolio" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">MOD Main Building</a> in London, where the First Sea Lord, also known as the Chief of the Naval Staff, is supported by the Naval Staff Department.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Commander" title="Fleet Commander">Fleet Commander</a> has responsibility for the provision of ships, submarines and aircraft ready for any operations that the Government requires. Fleet Commander exercises his authority through the <a href="/wiki/Navy_Command_Headquarters" class="mw-redirect" title="Navy Command Headquarters">Navy Command Headquarters</a>, based at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Excellent_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Excellent (shore establishment)">HMS&#160;<i>Excellent</i></a> in Portsmouth. An operational headquarters, the <a href="/wiki/Northwood_Headquarters" title="Northwood Headquarters">Northwood Headquarters</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Northwood,_London" title="Northwood, London">Northwood</a>, London, is co-located with the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Joint_Headquarters" title="Permanent Joint Headquarters">Permanent Joint Headquarters</a> of the United Kingdom\'s armed forces, and a NATO Regional Command, <a href="/wiki/Allied_Maritime_Command" title="Allied Maritime Command">Allied Maritime Command</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Royal Navy was the first of the three armed forces to combine the personnel and training command, under the Principal Personnel Officer, with the operational and policy command, combining the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief, Fleet and Naval Home Command into a single organisation, Fleet Command, in 2005 and becoming Navy Command in 2008. Within the combined command, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sea_Lord" title="Second Sea Lord">Second Sea Lord</a> continues to act as the Principal Personnel Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Naval Command senior appointments are:<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" cellpadding="5" style="margin:auto; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:left; width:15%;">Rank and class="mw-redirect" title="Chaplain of the Fleet">Chaplain of the Fleet</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Intelligence support to fleet operations is provided by intelligence sections at the various headquarters and from MOD <a href="/wiki/Defence_Intelligence" title="Defence Intelligence">Defence Intelligence</a>, renamed from the Defence Intelligence Staff in early 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/220px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/330px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg/440px-International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Fleet_Review._MOD_45144668.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> dockyard during the <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_200" class="mw-redirect" title="Trafalgar 200">Trafalgar 200</a> <a href="/wiki/International_Fleet_Review_2005" title="International Fleet Review 2005">International Fleet Review</a>. Seen here are commissioned ships from; the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Clyde.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/170px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/255px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/HMNB_Clyde.jpg/340px-HMNB_Clyde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Clyde.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">HMNB Clyde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faslane" class="mw-redirect" title="Faslane">Faslane</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Vanguard-class_submarine" title="Vanguard-class submarine"><i>Vanguard</i>-class</a> submarines</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Royal_Navy_shore_establishments" title="List of Royal Navy shore establishments">List of Royal Navy shore establishments</a></div>\n<p>The Royal Navy currently operates from three bases in the United Kingdom where commissioned ships are based; <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Clyde" title="HMNB Clyde">Clyde</a> and <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>\xe2\x80\x94Devonport is the largest operational naval base in the UK and Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Each base hosts a flotilla command under a <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(RN)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commodore (RN)">commodore</a>, or, in the case of Clyde, a captain, responsible for the provision of operational capability using the ships and submarines within the flotilla. <a href="/wiki/3_Commando_Brigade" title="3 Commando Brigade">3 Commando Brigade</a> Royal Marines is similarly commanded by a <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">brigadier</a> and based in Plymouth. Historically, the Royal Navy maintained <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_Dockyards" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Navy Dockyards">Royal Navy Dockyards</a> around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dockyard" class="mw-redirect" title="Dockyard">Dockyards</a> of the Royal Navy are harbours where ships are overhauled and refitted. Only four are operating today; at Devonport, <a href="/wiki/Faslane_Naval_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Faslane Naval Base">Faslane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosyth_Dockyard" title="Rosyth Dockyard">Rosyth</a> and at Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-UKNDABlackham_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKNDABlackham-197">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A Naval Base Review was undertaken in 2006 and early 2007, the outcome being announced by Secretary of State for Defence, <a href="/wiki/Des_Browne" title="Des Browne">Des Browne</a>, confirming that all would remain however some reductions in manpower were anticipated.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The academy where initial training for future Royal Navy officers takes place is Britannia Royal Naval College, located on a hill overlooking <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth,_Devon" title="Dartmouth, Devon">Dartmouth, Devon</a>. Basic training for future <a href="/wiki/Naval_rating" title="Naval rating">ratings</a> takes place at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Raleigh_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Raleigh (shore establishment)">HMS&#160;<i>Raleigh</i></a> at <a href="/wiki/Torpoint" title="Torpoint">Torpoint</a>, Cornwall, close to HMNB Devonport.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Significant numbers of naval personnel are employed within the Ministry of Defence, Defence Equipment and Support and on exchange with the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. Small numbers are also on exchange within other government departments and with allied fleets, such as the United States Navy. The navy also posts personnel in small units around the world to support ongoing operations and maintain standing commitments. Nineteen personnel are stationed in Gibraltar to support the small <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Squadron" title="Gibraltar Squadron">Gibraltar Squadron</a>, the RN\'s only permanent overseas squadron. A number of personnel are also based at East Cove Military Port and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Mount_Pleasant" title="RAF Mount Pleasant">RAF Mount Pleasant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> to support APT(S). Small numbers of personnel are based in <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a> (Naval Party 1002), Miami (NP 1011 \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/AUTEC" class="mw-redirect" title="AUTEC">AUTEC</a>), Singapore (NP 1022), <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> (NP 1023) and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> announced it would expand the UK\'s naval facilities in <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> to support larger Royal Navy ships deployed to the Persian Gulf. Once complete, it will be the UK\'s first permanent military base located <a href="/wiki/East_of_Suez" title="East of Suez">East of Suez</a> since it withdrew from the region in 1971. The base will reportedly be large enough to accommodate <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45</a> destroyers and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> aircraft carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_naming">Titles and naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Titles and naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/170px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/255px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg/340px-HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1947" data-file-height="2514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Richmond_MOD_45155880.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23 frigates</a> or "Duke class" are named after <a href="/wiki/Duke#United_Kingdom" title="Duke">British dukes</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Of_the_Navy">Of the Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Of the Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The navy of the United Kingdom is commonly referred to as the "Royal Navy" both in the United Kingdom and other countries. Navies of other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> countries <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">where the British monarch is also head of state</a> include their national name, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a>. Some navies of other monarchies, such as the <i>Koninklijke Marine</i> (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a>) and <i>Kungliga Flottan</i> (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Swedish Navy">Royal Swedish Navy</a>), are also called "Royal Navy" in their own language. The Danish Navy stands out with the term Royal incorporated in its official name (Royal Danish Navy), but only using the term "Fl\xc3\xa5den" (Navy) in everyday speech.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The French Navy, despite France being a republic since 1870, is often nicknamed <i>"La Royale"</i> (literally: The Royal).<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Of_ships">Of ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Of ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ships_of_the_Royal_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="List of ships of the Royal Navy">List of ships of the Royal Navy</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Royal_Navy_ships" title="List of active Royal Navy ships">List of active Royal Navy ships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naming_conventions_for_destroyers_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Naming conventions for destroyers of the Royal Navy">Naming conventions for destroyers of the Royal Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Type_system_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Type system of the Royal Navy">Type system of the Royal Navy</a></div>\n<p>Royal Navy ships in commission are prefixed since 1789 with <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Ship" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Ship">Her Majesty\'s Ship</a> (<a href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Ship" class="mw-redirect" title="His Majesty&#39;s Ship">His Majesty\'s Ship</a>), abbreviated to "HMS"; for example, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS&#160;<i>Beagle</i></a>. Submarines are styled HM Submarine, also abbreviated "HMS". Names are allocated to ships and submarines by a naming committee within the MOD and given by class, with the names of ships within a class often being thematic (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Type_23_frigate" title="Type 23 frigate">Type 23s</a> are named after <a href="/wiki/Duke#United_Kingdom" title="Duke">British dukes</a>) or traditional (for example, the <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Invincible-class aircraft carrier"><i>Invincible</i>-class&#x20;aircraft carriers</a> all carry the names of famous historic ships). Names are frequently re-used, offering a new ship the rich heritage, battle honours and traditions of her predecessors. Often, a particular vessel class will be named after the first ship of that type to be built. As well as a name, each ship and submarine of the Royal Navy and the Royal Fleet Auxiliary is given a <a href="/wiki/Pennant_number" title="Pennant number">pennant number</a> which in part denotes its role. For example, the destroyer <a href="/wiki/HMS_Daring_(D32)" title="HMS Daring (D32)">HMS&#160;<i>Daring</i></a> displays the pennant number \'D32\'.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Ranks.2C_rates.2C_and_Insignia"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranks,_rates,_and_Insignia">Ranks, rates, and Insignia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ranks, rates, and Insignia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_uniform" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Navy uniform">Royal Navy uniform</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_ranks,_rates,_and_uniforms_of_the_18th_and_19th_centuries" title="Royal Navy ranks, rates, and uniforms of the 18th and 19th centuries">Royal Navy ranks, rates, and uniforms of the 18th and 19th centuries</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_officer_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy officer rank insignia">Royal Navy officer rank insignia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_ratings_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy ratings rank insignia">Royal Navy ratings rank insignia</a></div>\n<p>The Royal Navy ranks, rates and insignia form part of the uniform of the Royal Navy.  The Royal Navy uniform is the pattern on which many of the uniforms of the other national navies of the world are based (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Ranks_and_insignia_of_NATO_navies_officers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers">Ranks and insignia of NATO navies officers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Uniforms of the United States Navy">Uniforms of the United States Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_Royal_Canadian_Navy" title="Uniforms of the Royal Canadian Navy">Uniforms of the Royal Canadian Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Navy#Uniforms" title="French Navy">French Naval Uniforms</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For officers (see also <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_officer_rank_insignia" title="Royal Navy officer rank insignia">Royal Navy officer rank insignia</a>):\n</p>\n<table style="border:1px solid #8888aa; background:#f7f8ff; id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Royal Navy has the following branch of service badges:\n</p>\n<table border="0" style="margin:auto; width:50%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="50%"><a href="/wiki/File:FleetAirArm_wings.jpg" title="File:FleetAirArm wings.jpg">Link to image</a>\n</th>\n<th width="50%"><div class="center"><div submariner.</center>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Custom_and_tradition">Custom and tradition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Custom and tradition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8f/Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="220" data-file-height="210" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_v_pd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">The Queen</a> and Admiral Sir Alan West during a <a href="/wiki/Fleet_review_(Commonwealth_realms)" title="Fleet review (Commonwealth realms)">Fleet Review</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Customs_and_traditions_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="Customs and traditions of the Royal Navy">Customs and traditions of the Royal Navy</a></div>\n<p>The Royal Navy has several formal customs and traditions including the use of ensigns and ships badges. Royal Navy ships have several ensigns used when under way and when in port. Commissioned ships and submarines wear the <a href="/wiki/White_Ensign" title="White Ensign">White Ensign</a> at the stern whilst alongside during daylight hours and at the main-mast whilst under way. When alongside, the <i>Union Jack</i> is flown from the <a href="/wiki/Jackstaff" title="Jackstaff">jackstaff</a> at the bow, and can only be flown under way either to signal a court-martial is in progress or to indicate the presence of an admiral of the fleet on-board (including the Lord High Admiral or the monarch).<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Review,_Royal_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Fleet Review, Royal Navy">Fleet Review</a> is an irregular tradition of assembling the fleet before the monarch. The first review on record was held in 1400, and the most recent review as of  2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> was held on 28 June 2005 to mark the bi-centenary of the Battle of Trafalgar; 167 ships from many different nations attended with the Royal Navy supplying 67.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are several less formal traditions including service nicknames and Naval slang. The nicknames include "The Andrew" (of uncertain origin, possibly after a zealous <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">press ganger</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> and "The Senior Service".<sup id="cite_ref-jackspeak_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jackspeak-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The RN has evolved a rich volume of slang, known as "Jack-speak". Nowadays the British sailor is usually "Jack" (or "Jenny") rather than the more historical "<a href="/wiki/Jack_Tar" title="Jack Tar">Jack Tar</a>". Royal Marines are fondly known as "Bootnecks" or often just as "Royals". A compendium of Naval slang was brought together by Commander A. Covey-Crump and his name has in itself become the subject of Naval slang; <a href="/wiki/Covey_Crump" title="Covey Crump">Covey Crump</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jackspeak_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jackspeak-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> A game traditionally played by the Navy is the four-player board game "<a href="/wiki/Uckers" title="Uckers">Uckers</a>". This is similar to <a href="/wiki/Ludo_(board_game)" title="Ludo (board game)">Ludo</a> and it is regarded as easy to learn, but difficult to play well.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Navy_Cadets">Navy Cadets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Navy Cadets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Royal Navy sponsors or supports four youth organisations:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Volunteer_Cadet_Corps" title="Volunteer Cadet Corps">Volunteer Cadet Corps</a> \xe2\x80\x93 consisting of Royal Naval Cadets and Royal Marines Cadets, the VCC was the first youth organisation officially supported or sponsored by the Admiralty in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Combined_Cadet_Force" title="Combined Cadet Force">Combined Cadet Force</a> \xe2\x80\x93 consisting of Naval cadets although now under the operational command of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sea_Cadets" title="Sea Cadets">Sea Cadets</a> \xe2\x80\x93 supporting teenagers who are interested in naval matters.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The above organisations are the responsibility of the CUY branch of Commander Core Training and Recruiting (COMCORE) who reports to <a href="/wiki/Flag_Officer_Sea_Training" title="Flag Officer Sea Training">Flag Officer Sea Training</a> (FOST).<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nautical_fiction" title="Nautical fiction">Nautical fiction</a></div>\n<p>The Royal Navy of the 18th century is depicted in many <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty_(novel)" title="Mutiny on the Bounty (novel)">novels</a> and several films dramatising the voyage and <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">mutiny on the Bounty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Navy\'s Napoleonic campaigns of the early 19th century are also a popular subject of historical novels. Some of the best-known are <a href="/wiki/Patrick_O%27Brian" title="Patrick O&#39;Brian">Patrick O\'Brian</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Aubrey-Maturin_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Aubrey-Maturin series">Aubrey-Maturin series</a><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/C._S._Forester" title="C. S. Forester">C. S. Forester</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Hornblower" title="Horatio Hornblower">Horatio Hornblower</a> chronicles.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Navy can also be seen in numerous films. The fictional spy <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> is "officially" a commander in the Royal Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Navy is featured in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me_(film)" title="The Spy Who Loved Me (film)">The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i>, when a nuclear ballistic-missile submarine is stolen,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> and in <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">Tomorrow Never Dies</a></i> when a media baron sinks a Royal Navy warship in an attempt to trigger a war between the UK and People\'s Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Master_and_Commander:_The_Far_Side_of_the_World" title="Master and Commander: The Far Side of the World">Master and Commander: The Far Side of the World</a></i> was based on Patrick O\'Brian\'s Aubrey-Maturin series.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean" title="Pirates of the Caribbean">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i> series of films also includes the Navy as the force pursuing the eponymous pirates.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/No%C3%ABl_Coward" title="No\xc3\xabl Coward">No\xc3\xabl Coward</a> directed and starred in his own film <i><a href="/wiki/In_Which_We_Serve" title="In Which We Serve">In Which We Serve</a></i>, which tells the story of the crew of the fictional HMS <i>Torrin</i> during the Second World War. It was intended as a propaganda film and was released in 1942. Coward starred as the ship\'s <a href="/wiki/Captain_(naval)" title="Captain (naval)">captain</a>, with supporting roles from <a href="/wiki/John_Mills" title="John Mills">John Mills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Richard Attenborough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>C. S. Forester\'s Hornblower novels have been <a href="/wiki/Hornblower_(TV_series)" title="Hornblower (TV series)">adapted for television</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Navy was the subject of an acclaimed 1970s <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television drama series, <i><a href="/wiki/Warship_(TV_series)" title="Warship (TV series)">Warship</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> and of a five-part documentary, <i>Shipmates</i>, that followed the workings of the Royal Navy day to day.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Television documentaries about the Royal Navy include: <i>Empire of the Seas: How the Navy Forged the Modern World</i>, a four-part documentary depicting Britain\'s rise as a naval superpower, up until the First World War;<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sailor_(TV_series)" title="Sailor (TV series)">Sailor</a></i>, about life on the aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(R09)" title="HMS Ark Royal (R09)">HMS&#160;<i>Ark Royal</i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Submarine</i>, about the <a href="/wiki/Submarine_Command_Course" title="Submarine Command Course">submarine captains\' training course</a>, \'The Perisher\'.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> There have also been Channel 5 documentaries such as <i>Royal Navy Submarine Mission</i>, following a nuclear-powered fleet submarine.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The popular BBC radio comedy series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Navy_Lark" title="The Navy Lark">The Navy Lark</a></i> featured a fictitious warship ("HMS <i>Troutbridge</i>") and ran from 1959 to 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Comedy:_The_Navy_Lark_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Comedy:_The_Navy_Lark-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English Empire</a><small> (until 1707)</small></li><li><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> <small> (until 1707)</small></li><li><a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a><small> (1707 \xe2\x80\x93 20th century)</small></li></ul></div></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since April 2013, MoD publications no longer report the entire strength of the <a href="/wiki/Regular_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Regular Reserve (United Kingdom)">Regular Reserve</a>, instead, only Regular Reserves serving under a fixed-term reserve contract are counted. These contracts are similar in nature to the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Maritime Reserve (United Kingdom)">Maritime Reserve</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Royal Navy parlance, "commissioned ships" invariably refers to both <a href="/wiki/Submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="Submarines">submarines</a> and surface ships. Non-commissioned ships operated by or in support of <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Naval_Service" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Naval Service">Her Majesty\'s Naval Service</a> are not included.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><style
